## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor concentration ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard state-variable form for chemical kinetics in well-mixed (0D) reactors. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are rate laws where dA_dt depends on A via reaction order, saturation/inhibition-like nonlinearities, or explicit time-varying rate coefficients/forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate generation/consumption over a time window)
- First-order decay/growth: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay if c0<0; autocatalytic growth if c0>0)
- nth-order power-law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general mass-action order with respect to A)
- Mixed-order (polynomial) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A**3 (sum of multiple pathways approximated by a polynomial in A)
- Autocatalysis with depletion (logistic-type in A): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplifying growth limited by finite capacity/depletion)
- Reversible-like relaxation to equilibrium level: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (linear return toward steady concentration c1)
- Rational self-inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate increases with A at low A and levels off at high A due to self-limitation/transport limits)
- Substrate inhibition / high-A slowdown: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate increases then decreases/levels off at high A due to inhibition/aggregation)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (linearly drifting effective rate constant due to temperature ramp/catalyst deactivation)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * A (externally modulated rate constant, e.g., light-driven/oscillatory conditions)
- Non-autonomous source/sink: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (baseline kinetics plus a time-dependent feed/side-source term)
- Finite-time quench/activation (smooth switch): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (1 + tanh(c2 * (t - c3))) (rate regime changes around t≈c3, e.g., catalyst activation/quench)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line in dA_dt vs A at fixed t), it indicates effective first-order kinetics with slope = c0 (possibly time-varying if slope changes with t).
- If dA_dt vs A is a power curve on log-log axes (approximately linear), it suggests a mass-action form dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 where c1 is the apparent reaction order.
- A stable steady state A* is indicated by a sign change in dA_dt around A* (dA_dt>0 for A<A*, dA_dt<0 for A>A*), consistent with relaxation forms like c0*(c1-A) or c0*A*(c1-A).
- A rate that increases with A at low A but approaches a ceiling at high A suggests a rational saturation form such as c0 * A / (c1 + A).
- A rate that rises then falls (or strongly flattens) at high A suggests self-inhibition/aggregation, often captured by extra A**2 terms in the denominator (e.g., c0*A/(c1+A+c2*A**2)) or negative higher-order polynomial terms.
- If dA_dt depends on t even when A is held similar (e.g., at the same A, different times give different dA_dt), the system is likely non-autonomous with explicit t dependence in coefficients or additive source terms.
- Abrupt regime changes in the time series (different kinetic behavior before/after a time) often correspond to smooth switching terms like tanh(c*(t-c0)) multiplying a kinetic component.
- Oscillatory patterns in dA_dt at similar A values (repeating in time) suggest periodic forcing in the rate coefficient, often appearing as sin(c*t+c0) modulating A-dependent kinetics.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK4)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_q*A*log(c3*t + c4)
Candidate formulas: 87

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,A)= -0.1149290460\,A^2 \;+\; 0.06806555110\,A\cdot \log(0.2569297861\,t+1).
\]
So any matching candidate must be exactly of the form
\[
(\text{constant})\cdot A^2 \;+\; (\text{constant})\cdot A\log(\text{affine in }t),
\]
with **no extra dependence** on \(t\) alone, no extra dependence on \(A\) alone (besides the \(A^2\) term), and no other nonlinearities (exp, sin, Max, rational terms, extra logs, etc.). Also the log argument must be \(c\,t+1\) (or equivalent), and the coefficient on the log term must be linear in \(A\) (exactly \(A\times\)constant).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether all “extra” terms can be zeroed out and whether the remaining structure can match the two GT terms.

---

### 1. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2(c3+t)^{c4} + c5\)
Has \(Ac1\) (linear in \(A\)) and a power term \(A(c3+t)^{c4}\), not a log. Cannot become \(A\log(\cdot)\) for all \(t\). **No**.

### 2. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + Ac3\max(0,c4+t)\)
The Max term cannot equal 0 for all \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Setting \(c3=0\) leaves \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1)\), which matches GT form. Choose \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c1=0.06806555110\), \(c2=0.2569297861\). **Yes**.

### 3. \(A^2c0 + A^2c1 + Ac2\log(c3t+1)\)
Combine \(A^2(c0+c1)\) and match log term. Set \(c0+c1=-0.1149290460\) (many choices), \(c2=0.06806555110\), \(c3=0.2569297861\). **Yes**.

### 4. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1)\)
Exactly GT structure. Set \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c1=0.06806555110\), \(c2=0.2569297861\). **Yes**.

### 5. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + c3e^{c4t} + c5\)
Extra \(t\)-only exponential term. To remove for all \(t\): set \(c3=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then matches as in (4). **Yes**.

### 6. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + Ac3 e^{c4|c5-t|}\)
Extra \(A\cdot e^{(\cdot)}\) term. Must set \(c3=0\) to remove. Then matches (4). **Yes**.

### 7. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2/(c3t+c4) + Ac5 + Ac6\log(c7t+1) + c8 + c9/(c3t+c4)\)
To match GT, must eliminate: \(Ac1, Ac2/(...), Ac5, c8, c9/(...)\). Set \(c1=c2=c5=c8=c9=0\). Then left with \(A^2c0 + Ac6\log(c7t+1)\) which matches. Choose \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c6=0.06806555110\), \(c7=0.2569297861\). **Yes**.

### 8. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2/(c3t+c4) + A^{c5}c6\log(c7t+1) + c8 + c9/(c3t+c4)\)
Need \(A^{c5}c6\log(\cdot)\) to become \(A\cdot(\text{const})\log(\cdot)\): set \(c5=1\). Eliminate other extras by \(c1=c2=c8=c9=0\). Then match with \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c6=0.06806555110\), \(c7=0.2569297861\). **Yes**.

### 9. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + Ac3/(c4t+c5) + c6 + c7/(c4t+c5)\)
Extra rational-in-\(t\) terms and constant. Remove by \(c3=0, c6=0, c7=0\). Then matches (4). **Yes**.

### 10. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + c3 t (A+c4)^{c5}\)
Extra term \(t(A+c4)^{c5}\). Only removable by \(c3=0\). Then matches (4). **Yes**.

### 11. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + Ac3 + Ac4 t\)
Extra \(A\) and \(At\) terms. Remove with \(c3=0, c4=0\). Then matches (4). **Yes**.

### 12. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + Ac3(c4+t)^{c5}\)

### 13. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2t+1) + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6\)
